class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Europe</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png/330px-Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png" width="330" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png/495px-Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png/660px-Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png 2x" data-file-width="1268" data-file-height="996" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_Asia_transcontinental.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #67e836; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;States entirely within conventional Europe</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #9ac0ea; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Transcontinental territory most often considered to be within Europe</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5d66be; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Transcontinental territory most often considered to be outside Europe</div>  <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #945dbe; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Geographically Asian states (including <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>)</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The list below includes all entities falling even partially under any of the <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Europe" title="Regions of Europe">various common definitions of Europe</a>, geographical or political. Fifty-six sovereign states, six of which have limited recognition, are listed with territory in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and/or membership in international European organisations. There are eight areas that are not integral parts of a European state or have special political status.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Geographical_boundaries_of_Europe"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Geographical boundaries of Europe</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Sovereign_states"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Sovereign states</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Recognised_states"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Recognised states</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#States_with_limited_recognition"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">States with limited recognition</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Dependent_territories"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Dependent territories</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Special_areas_of_internal_sovereignty"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Special areas of internal sovereignty</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_boundaries_of_Europe">Geographical boundaries of Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geographical boundaries of Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boundaries_between_the_continents_of_Earth" title="Boundaries between the continents of Earth">Boundaries between the continents of Earth</a></div>\n<p>Under the commonly used geographic definition, the <a href="/wiki/Boundaries_between_the_continents_of_Earth" title="Boundaries between the continents of Earth">border</a> between <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> stretches along the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> in the east,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Greater Caucasus</a> range<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, with its outlets, the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a>, in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Based on that division, <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental states</a> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> have territory both in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> is proximate to <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asia Minor</a>), but often considered part of Europe and is a current member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU). <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> is also entirely in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> but is a member of certain European organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> provides a clearer divide between <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, some traditionally European islands such as <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantelleria" title="Pantelleria">Pantelleria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pelagian_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelagian Islands">Pelagian Islands</a> are located on the African continental plate.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The island of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a>, straddling the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some territories geographically outside Europe have strong connections with European states. <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> has socio-political connections with Europe and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>, but closer to the continent of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and usually grouped with it.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Sometimes <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> is considered as part of <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Europe" title="Regions of Europe">geopolitical Europe</a> as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Other territories are part of European countries but are geographically located in other continents, such as the <a href="/wiki/French_overseas_departments" class="mw-redirect" title="French overseas departments">French overseas departments</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> the Spanish cities of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> on the coast of Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">Dutch Caribbean</a> territories of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Netherlands_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Netherlands-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_countries_map_en_2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Europe_countries_map_en_2.png/220px-Europe_countries_map_en_2.png" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Europe_countries_map_en_2.png/330px-Europe_countries_map_en_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Europe_countries_map_en_2.png/440px-Europe_countries_map_en_2.png 2x" data-file-width="1473" data-file-height="1198" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_countries_map_en_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Political map of Europe and the surrounding region</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sovereign_states">Sovereign states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Sovereign states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> is a political association with effective <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> over a population for whom it makes decisions in the national interest.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Montevideo_convention" class="mw-redirect" title="Montevideo convention">Montevideo convention</a>, a state must have a permanent population, a defined territory, a government, and the capacity to enter into relations with other states.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognised_states">Recognised states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recognised states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are 50 internationally recognised sovereign states with territory located within the common definition of Europe and/or membership in international European organisations, of which 44 have their <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> within Europe. All except the Vatican City are members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and all except Belarus, Kazakhstan and Vatican City are members of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> 28 of these countries have also been <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states of the EU</a> since 2013, which means they are highly integrated with each other and share their sovereignty with <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">EU institutions</a>.\n</p><p>Each entry in the list below has a map of its location in Europe. Territory in Europe is shown in dark-green; territory not geographically in Europe is shown in a lighter shade of green. The lightest shade of green represents states in the EU and is shown on the maps of all territories within the EU.\n</p>\n<table>\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="background:lightcyan; border:1px solid id="States_with_limited_recognition">States with limited recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: States with limited recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following six entities in Europe have partial <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">diplomatic recognition</a> by one or more <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN member states</a> (and therefore are defined as states by the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state#Constitutive_theory" title="Sovereign state">constitutive theory of statehood</a>) or have no <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">diplomatic recognition</a> by any UN member state but are defined as states by the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state#Declarative_theory" title="Sovereign state">declarative theory of statehood</a> and are recognised by one or more Non-UN member states. None are members of the UN, Council of Europe or EU.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="width:100%">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="unsortable">Flag\n</th>\n<th href="/wiki/Timeline_of_European_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of European nations">Timeline of European nations</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div style=""><ol class="references" style="list-style-type:upper-alpha;">\n<li id="cnote_a">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_a_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_a_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_a_3">c</a> <a href="#ref_a_4">d</a> <a href="#ref_a_5">e</a> <a href="#ref_a_6">f</a></sup></b></i> Area and population numbers include integral areas located outside of Europe. The area and population of states with separatist regions includes that of the separatist regions.</li>\n<li id="cnote_b">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_b_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_b_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_b_3">c</a> <a href="#ref_b_4">d</a> <a href="#ref_b_5">e</a> <a href="#ref_b_6">f</a></sup></b></i> Part of the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasian Region</a>, at the crossroads of Europe and Asia. <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">Physiographically</a>, Armenia falls entirely in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, while Georgia and Azerbaijan are mostly in Asia with small portions north of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> divide in Europe.</li>\n<li id="cnote_c">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_c_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_c_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_c_3">c</a></sup></b></i> The island of Cyprus is located on the Cyprian arc on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_Plate" title="Anatolian Plate">Anatolian Plate</a> and is <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">physiographically</a> associated with Asia, but it is part of European organisations such as the EU.</li>\n<li id="cnote_d"><b><a href="#ref_d_1">^</a></b> The terms <i>Republic of Ireland</i> and <i>Poblacht na h\xc3\x89ireann</i> are not official long names and are used only as a legal description meant to differentiate the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">state</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">island</a>.</li>\n<li id="cnote_e">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_e_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_e_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_e_3">c</a></sup></b></i> Kazakhstan, Russia and Turkey have territory in both Europe (dark green) and Asia (light green).</li>\n<li id="cnote_f">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_f_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_f_2">b</a></sup></b></i> <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> are <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent countries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Realm">Kingdom of Denmark</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> respectively. Both are members of the EU; however, the other constituent countries of their kingdoms are not. In international organisations, the terms Denmark and the Netherlands are often used as short names for their respective kingdoms as a whole.</li>\n<li id="cnote_g"><b><a href="#ref_g_1">^</a></b> The Netherlands is also known as "Holland", but this name properly refers only to a <a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">region</a> of the country. See <a href="/wiki/Terminology_of_the_Low_Countries" title="Terminology of the Low Countries">Netherlands (terminology)</a>.</li>\n<li id="cnote_h">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_h_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_h_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_h_3">c</a> <a href="#ref_h_4">d</a></sup></b></i> The United Kingdom consists of the <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">countries</a> of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>. The UK is responsible for the foreign relations and ultimate good governance of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a> of Guernsey, the Isle of Man and Jersey, which are otherwise separate. England, Scotland and Wales make up the island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> (or simply Britain), which is sometimes used synonymously with the United Kingdom.</li>\n<li id="cnote_i">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_i_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_i_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_i_3">c</a> <a href="#ref_i_4">d</a> <a href="#ref_i_5">e</a> <a href="#ref_i_6">f</a></sup></b></i> <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">EU candidate country</a>.</li>\n<li id="cnote_j"><b><a href="#ref_j_1">^</a></b> A simpler official short name has been encouraged by the Czech government, "<i>Czechia</i>". By 2017, this variant remains uncommon. Nevertheless, this term has been adopted by several companies and organisations, including Google Maps, instead of the term "<i>Czech Republic</i>". See <a href="/wiki/Name_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Name of the Czech Republic">Name of the Czech Republic</a>.</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Charles T.
